<review>If you're interested in trying out Mediterranean-style food (basically an amalgamation of Greek and various Arabic cuisines) for the first time, this is your place to go.

The food is healthy (loaded with vegetables and legumes) and yet delicious at the same time, in a form factor that's palatable to the general populace. I have tried the wrap and box with various proteins, and my favorite food would be the saffron rice (it has a good aroma and I'd eat an entire plate of just that). The falafels are well spiced and crunchy, and the meat is pretty good too. Meals from the places are hearty yet balanced, with a good harmony between the salad, rice, proteins, and sauce. Just be sure to load up on garlic yogurt to make everything better, and choose pickled onions.

A gripe I have though is that the food is a little pricey, but I think it's still worth it. After eating from this place, it makes me desire to have more restaurants like this where I live, in National City. It's super healthy yet delicious, which is not something common among restaurants here (all I see here is the typical unhealthy fast food). I also just like this sort of cuisine. Even then, I still make 25 minute trips to order from The Kebab Shop, which I'd definitely make more often if there were more restaurants like this closer to me. I'm just kind of sad that they're only in East County or more affluent areas.

In general, this is a place where you won't regret coming to.</review><Pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipN6ggRJMvqzPhf9QXVxaDSSPmNsYyXLFxURBBdD=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOwq09oAGfWB6btppwocllqx-h7wH359rcJamQ4=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//Pictures>< response>

< review>
As good as the original The Kebab Shop in downtown San Diego, which I had reviewed it first.
In contrast to the one in downtown, it seems to be average in terms of business (i.e. people come but not that many), it is way more spacious than it looks like from the outside so it can, theoretically-speaking, hold a lot of people, and it is also one of the cleanest places I have seen around eastern Chula Vista or so.

Not to mention it is quite close to the Otay Ranch bus station so it is a good place for those who live around the eastern parts of the South Bay or so.
I would definitely recommend it, and I honestly hope it gets popular in order to not go that far from a place that serves great kebabs!<//review>

<username>Lauren Thomson</username><Time>1563538409397< /Time>< rating>
5</rating>
< Text>
Whereas many other top-tier LA pizza restaurants in town can come across as high-minded and haughty, there's a charming blue-collar vibe here. The crispy, char-crusted pizzas arrive on metal sheet pans, while the crushed garlic and Parmesan sit in serve-yourself caddies just in front of the open kitchen. Order the Margherita - simply dressed with melted buffalo mozzarella, imported crushed tomatoes, basil and a smidge of garlic - and it becomes apparent that this humble operation takes its pizza as serious any other operation in town.< /Text>
